<div id="review_1219557149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219557149" />
    <a title="P. Kirby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112326-p-kirby"><img alt="P. Kirby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442534274p2/5112326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219557149?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P. Kirby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="P. Kirby" href="/user/show/5112326-p-kirby">P. Kirby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13172241-possessing-the-secret-of-joy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112326-p-kirby?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219557149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13961408211351996468">There's no question that a practice that mutilates women with the goal of making them look like Barbie dolls--i.e., with a flat, featureless landscape instead of actual genitalia--is inhumane and nothing that should be condoned as "tradition." The problem, however, with <i>Possessing the Secret Joy</i>, a novel about Tashi, a woman who has suffered this brutal practice and continues to struggle with the physical and emotional scars for many decades after, is that the narrative structure is messy and la</span>
  <span id="freeText13961408211351996468" style="display:none">There's no question that a practice that mutilates women with the goal of making them look like Barbie dolls--i.e., with a flat, featureless landscape instead of actual genitalia--is inhumane and nothing that should be condoned as "tradition." The problem, however, with <i>Possessing the Secret Joy</i>, a novel about Tashi, a woman who has suffered this brutal practice and continues to struggle with the physical and emotional scars for many decades after, is that the narrative structure is messy and lacks the emotional power I expected.<br /><br />The story is told in alternating POVs (one per chapter): Tashi, her husband Adam, their son Benny, Tashi's friend, Tashi's shrink, Adam's mistress (yes, his mistress), and Adam's son with the mistress. There may be another POV in there, as well. After a while, the various voices in the novel started to blur--none are particularly well-defined or possess unique character. The story also tries to address other issues beyond female genital mutilation--AIDs, the colonization of Africa by Western powers, etc. All issues worth exploring, but again, the narrative structure is so unstructured, that the message gets lost in the method.<br /><br />The basic plot follows the "mystery" of Tashi's crime, the why and how she came to be imprisoned in an African jail, despite her obvious American citizenship. The slow unfolding of this mystery is the only thing that kept me reading. Tashi, herself, is too much the unreliable narrator. I get what Walker was trying to do; demonstrate the extent to which Tashi struggles with a sense of self, but...I never connected with her. <br /><br />I confess, Tashi's "circumcision," performed with her consent, as an adult, didn't move me as much as it should have. Tashi's motivation, to appease a messiah-like political figure, to prove her African-ness, seemed inadequate. And yes, I know that's the mindset of a privileged Western woman talking, but still...Tashi's plight didn't move me as much as that of the very young girls who are forced to undergo the mutilation.<br /><br />Nevertheless, <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i> is worth reading, if only for its value in shedding light on an absolutely abominable practice that quite literally cripples thousands of women in Africa and the Middle East. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13961408211351996468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_11624203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Tulara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/145359-tulara"><img alt="Tulara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184420632p2/145359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11624203?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tulara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tulara" href="/user/show/145359-tulara">Tulara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11624203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18057351578982795262">The book details the life of an African girl, Tashi, from her youth through marriage - she meets the son and a daughter of missionaries and becomes friends with them - although still seeking acceptance from her village. The author, Alice Walker, gives us a unique perspective for each of the characters in each chapter. We see the wonderful youthful girl enjoying a crush and feeling the splendor of sex in the grass - yet - we learn that women in that village practice genital circumcision on every </span>
  <span id="freeText18057351578982795262" style="display:none">The book details the life of an African girl, Tashi, from her youth through marriage - she meets the son and a daughter of missionaries and becomes friends with them - although still seeking acceptance from her village. The author, Alice Walker, gives us a unique perspective for each of the characters in each chapter. We see the wonderful youthful girl enjoying a crush and feeling the splendor of sex in the grass - yet - we learn that women in that village practice genital circumcision on every young girl. The book chronicles the history and the belief that women are unclean and that myths and practices destroy the person within. Tashi's struggles with her inner demons - trying to connect with the traditions that define her as a member of the village, with the knowledge that the practice killed her sister, Dura.<br />Powerfully written, you are standing beside Tashi as she descends into madness and with Adam, her husband, as he tries to find a common ground but also has a mistress when Tashi's actions push him away.<br />I learned more about how this practice destroys the very women who practice it - bound by village patriarchy. The book reached an explosive breaking point when Tashi meets the woman who performed her "rite." Years later, the woman has been raised to a public celebrity for another reason and Tashi goes to visit her.<br />Stunning writing - difficult and horrifying subject matter - it's a must read for women. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18057351578982795262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77499545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77499545" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1580003-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246235989p2/1580003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77499545?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/1580003-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781595583642" href="/book/show/2761997-possessing-the-secret-of-joy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77499545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14311392332161266451">Such a moving novel that centers around Tashi (from <i>The Color Purple</i> and the horrific custom of female genital mutilation. <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i> is, as far as I know, is the first novel to illustrate the beliefs, effects, practices, and horrors behind FGM. Tashi represents the "every woman" who takes a stand for women's rights, but only after she chooses to undergo circumcision as a young woman. The book is broken into many short chapters, each one narrated by a different character in the</span>
  <span id="freeText14311392332161266451" style="display:none">Such a moving novel that centers around Tashi (from <i>The Color Purple</i> and the horrific custom of female genital mutilation. <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i> is, as far as I know, is the first novel to illustrate the beliefs, effects, practices, and horrors behind FGM. Tashi represents the "every woman" who takes a stand for women's rights, but only after she chooses to undergo circumcision as a young woman. The book is broken into many short chapters, each one narrated by a different character in the book including Tashi, her husband, her sister-in-law, etc., which gives interesting perspective. <br /><br />Every woman ought to read this book, especially those living in their comfy and cozy American homes. In fact -- let me just get on my soapbox for a moment -- wake up! There are women in the U.S. who are opting to have this barbaric surgery done to them in order to feel a connection to their African or Asian roots. They are made to feel dirty and unclean if they are "not bathed." We must educate ourselves and then educate those around us to continue to fight for women's rights -- not just for equality, but to end <b>violence against women</b>. This, my friends, continues to be a global crisis in 2009. <br /><br />Anyway, definitely read <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i>. It's definitely one of those "profoundly moving books."<br /><br />(P.S. Claudia -- you definitely need to borrow this! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14311392332161266451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1021842735" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021842735" />
    <a title="Cylia Kamp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6706263-cylia-kamp"><img alt="Cylia Kamp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319040295p2/6706263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1021842735?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cylia Kamp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cylia Kamp" href="/user/show/6706263-cylia-kamp">Cylia Kamp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781595583642" href="/book/show/2761997-possessing-the-secret-of-joy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6706263-cylia-kamp?shelf=my-written-reviews">my-written-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1021842735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4117441071334182308">In 1991 Alice Walker first published the novel, <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i>. It introduced many readers to the ruthless, painful technique known as female genital mutilation (FMG) or female circumcision, suffered by 90 to 100 million women worldwide. Because the subject had long been taboo among those groups who practice it as well as throughout the rest of the world, the book was taken out of print. But fortunately for modern readers and current sufferers everywhere, Ms. Walker and others bega</span>
  <span id="freeText4117441071334182308" style="display:none">In 1991 Alice Walker first published the novel, <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i>. It introduced many readers to the ruthless, painful technique known as female genital mutilation (FMG) or female circumcision, suffered by 90 to 100 million women worldwide. Because the subject had long been taboo among those groups who practice it as well as throughout the rest of the world, the book was taken out of print. But fortunately for modern readers and current sufferers everywhere, Ms. Walker and others began to report even more thoroughly on the noxious anti-feminism and unusual folklore supporting the practice. Their actions and appeals resulted in the reissue of <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i> in 2008. Another factor driving the need for more information about FMG was the increasing numbers of immigrants crossing the US borders. Many were suffering from the consequences of the procedure. Physicians and staff running the US clinics which serve this population were soon in need of better treatment information. Thank goodness other books and conferences began popping up, and the horrors (both physical and psychological) and the treatments of the practice have been further revealed.<br /><br />I highly recommend this novel not only for its information but also for its startling truth and dramatic storytelling. Be aware, though, presentation of the details of the procedure and its possible consequences are not sugar coated.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4117441071334182308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132736125" />
    <a title="Martha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13381865-martha"><img alt="Martha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548742208p2/13381865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132736125?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martha" href="/user/show/13381865-martha">Martha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132736125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10022045303146587326">I have never written a review before but after reading this I feel like I can't not say anything. This book made me feel so much and so intensely, I know the story is a work of fiction but the events and the horror that happens in the book is so terribly factual that it made me feel sick whilst reading it.<br/>It is a fast read in terms of content, however I could not sit for hours at a time because it took energy from me; I found myself taking regular breaks to reflect and, if I'm honest, cry. <br/>The t</span>
  <span id="freeText10022045303146587326" style="display:none">I have never written a review before but after reading this I feel like I can't not say anything. This book made me feel so much and so intensely, I know the story is a work of fiction but the events and the horror that happens in the book is so terribly factual that it made me feel sick whilst reading it.<br />It is a fast read in terms of content, however I could not sit for hours at a time because it took energy from me; I found myself taking regular breaks to reflect and, if I'm honest, cry. <br />The taboo and ignorance around FGM is something I have been part of for a long time and have only recently become aware of. Alice Walker not only opens your eyes to the reality and the presence of it within societies all over the world, but she also attempts to communicate the endless suffering and madness caused by this horrifying 'tradition'.<br />I feel like I can't quite eloquently put into words the way the book made me feel and what it made me think. I believe this is one of the first true trauma narratives I have read, at least it is the first to have truly impacted me.<br />This book is so important, because it forces you to face something which is so hidden in society and because it touches you and moves you through the beautiful language and very human characters.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10022045303146587326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1771721559902548372">Very disjointed, character-driven story telling in which the plot itself is a mystery that is slowly revealed by numerous, inter-related characters at various points in time. <div id="review_3373533190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373533190" />
    <a title="Veronica  Gavilanes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66037874-veronica-gavilanes"><img alt="Veronica  Gavilanes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590437949p2/66037874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3373533190?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica  Gavilanes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica  Gavilanes" href="/user/show/66037874-veronica-gavilanes">Veronica  Gavilanes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671789428" href="/book/show/538538.Possessing_the_Secret_of_Joy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66037874-veronica-gavilanes?shelf=desaf%C3%ADo-2020">desafío-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3373533190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14829322322587167794">"And that the God of women is autonomy" <br/><br/>This book follows the story of Tashi (later Christianized and called Evelyn), an Olinka woman from a fictional African nation, who becomes close to a missionary family from the United States since childhood. She is the best friend of Olivia, the daughter of the missionaries, and years later marries Adam, the son of that family, so she moves to their country. She loves the United States, but she has physical and emotional issues that lead her to spend weeks</span>
  <span id="freeText14829322322587167794" style="display:none">"And that the God of women is autonomy" <br /><br />This book follows the story of Tashi (later Christianized and called Evelyn), an Olinka woman from a fictional African nation, who becomes close to a missionary family from the United States since childhood. She is the best friend of Olivia, the daughter of the missionaries, and years later marries Adam, the son of that family, so she moves to their country. She loves the United States, but she has physical and emotional issues that lead her to spend weeks in a psychiatric facility over the years while her husband travels to visit his friend and mistress. After decades of therapy, she realizes that the origins of her problems are the death of her sister Dura after she was circumcised as a child and her own genital mutilation (she was not forced into it, but she chose it to honor her roots). This is the story of Tashi/Evelyn, her process of understanding how much genital mutilation broke her, and how she tries to deal with it and heal.<br /><br />What I liked: I learned a lot about genital mutilation, the physical consequences of it, and the cultural origins of this practice. I do understand this is not a medical, anthropological, or psychological text, nor is it a true experience, but it works very well for fiction, as it encourages the readers to make questions. The author portraited the point of view of each character, so I liked that the reader can have insight from each of them, as it allows a better comprehension of the story. I loved the tales at the beginning of the book, and I also enjoyed the conclusion. This is an empowering book because it shows that strength can be found in our flaws, struggles, and issues. It is also a love letter for the vulva and women's pleasure, which is necessary. <br /><br />What I did not like: Even when I liked understanding each character, their subjectivity, their motivations, and their version of the story, all of them are written in the same way, so the style is too monotone for a multiple viewpoint novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14829322322587167794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('23U/B3kRJxYAlnvuyOZ1xSnCcc8iyCjggyqZuQLxxkq71HFVG2c57tTvK3iOguBC1e6YJ6iCU/XuznKWR2foDA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17133654474525759923">Alice Walker, one of the United States’ preeminent writers, is an award-winning author of novels, stories, essays, and poetry. In 1983, Walker became the first African-American woman to win a Pulitzer Prize for fiction with her novel <i>The Color Purple</i>, which also won the National Book Award. Her other books include <i>The Third Life of Grange Copeland</i>, <i>Meridian</i>, <i>The Temple of My Familiar</i>, and <i>Possessi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17133654474525759923" style="display:none">Alice Walker, one of the United States’ preeminent writers, is an award-winning author of novels, stories, essays, and poetry. In 1983, Walker became the first African-American woman to win a Pulitzer Prize for fiction with her novel <i>The Color Purple</i>, which also won the National Book Award. Her other books include <i>The Third Life of Grange Copeland</i>, <i>Meridian</i>, <i>The Temple of My Familiar</i>, and <i>Possessing the Secret of Joy</i>. In her public life, Walker has worked to address problems of injustice, inequality, and poverty as an activist, teacher, and public intellectual.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17133654474525759923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
